  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4274565e-cacd-4b49-8d80-bf863b650586'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/853602-i-am-just-starting-reading-comics-and">I am just starting reading comics, and have only Xmen Movies as my reference for these characters. Should I start with something else before diving into this? I have only checked out the first dozen pages but I feel like I need some more exposition. Should I dig in or is there another set of this series I should start with? Thanks!</a>
</div>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/39143866-tracey-newport"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1421212744i/39143866._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/39143866-tracey-newport">Tracey Newport</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I would recommend starting somewhere else. If you are just going off the movies several things might be a little confusing. I would recommend looking <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I would recommend starting somewhere else. If you are just going off the movies several things might be a little confusing. I would recommend looking up a guide or so to help you navigate marvel. I personally have been using this guide: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.comicbookherald.com/the-complete-marvel-reading-order-guide/knights-until-avengers-disassembled/">http://www.comicbookherald.com/the-co...</a> There are several things in here that help and so far most have been pretty good. I only deviated from this list by those I couldn't find and reading the many infinity stories with Thanos.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_45819451" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45819451" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45819451?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=superhero">superhero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=2016-reread">2016-reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=marvel">marvel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45819451" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8481134149459810273">Grant Morrison did an ambitious run on <i>New X-Men</i>, but that story had to be walked back in the interests of continuing it in on-going mainstream superhero comics. Marvel made a wise choice when they tapped Joss Whedon, lord of the TV geeks back then, to help get the X-Men out of the black leather and back into spandex. (It’s reasonable to assume that his work here was a big reason that he’d later get the gig writing and directing the <i>Avengers</i> movies.)<br/><br/>Kitty Pryde returns to the school as Cyclops i</span>
  <span id="freeText8481134149459810273" style="display:none">Grant Morrison did an ambitious run on <i>New X-Men</i>, but that story had to be walked back in the interests of continuing it in on-going mainstream superhero comics. Marvel made a wise choice when they tapped Joss Whedon, lord of the TV geeks back then, to help get the X-Men out of the black leather and back into spandex. (It’s reasonable to assume that his work here was a big reason that he’d later get the gig writing and directing the <i>Avengers</i> movies.)<br /><br />Kitty Pryde returns to the school as Cyclops is forming a new team with the goal to promote the mutant cause by putting a flashy group out in public that would be more like the better known superheroes than a bunch of underground militant activists. Hence, the return of the tights. No sooner does the line-up get set than they get word that a scientists has created a so-called cure to the mutant gene that causes a variety of ethical debates as well as fear of what that could do in the wrong hands. This happens just as a new alien villain called Ord starts causing trouble. Oh, and a character comes back from the grave because nobody stays dead in comic books.<br /><br />I admit that even though I’m a huge fan of Whedon that I had a few reservations about this when I first read it about ten years ago. I grumbled about the return to a more baseline version after Morrison’s mind-bending run seemed to offer new and bold directions, and I really disliked yet another instance of a dead X-Man pulling a Lazarus. <br /><br />However, my inner comic fanboy doesn’t rage quite as hard against that particular machine these days. I’ve come to accept that continuity can provide a useful foundation, but that it too often becomes a crushing weight that overwhelms stories so I tend to think of each particular era as a self-contained bubble of a story. Once I accepted that I was a much happier comic book fan overall. <br /><br />So in my head canon Morrison’s run is one version of the X-Men, Whedon’s is another, and Whedon’s run is pretty great. The look and tone of the <i>X-Men</i> movies had infiltrated the comics to some degree, but now a decade’s worth of superhero films has shown us that you can make them colorful and fun after all. (At least they can be if they’re not directed by Zach Snyder.) So putting a team back in bright costumes and having them fight a genocidal alien makes me think that Whedon was a bit ahead of the curve on this idea of letting comic books be comic books. At the same time the storyline of the mutant cure puts the social issues of bigotry and tolerance that the X-titles represent front and center, too.<br /><br />There’s also great dramatic tension among this team with Wolverine pissed off at Cyclops for taking up with Emma Frost so soon after Jean Grey’s latest death. Kitty doesn’t trust Emma because she doesn’t buy the reformed villain act. Emma thinks everyone but her is a naïve idiot. Beast is conflicted about the idea of a cure and a chance to be fully human again which infuriates Wolverine who believes that no X-Man should reject their status as mutant. All of this is dealt with in both physical and verbal fights, and of course the Whedon dialogue laces all of this with plenty of humor.<br /><br />Overall, this a really solid comic with a serious storyline that doesn’t forget the fun factor.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8481134149459810273" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1360821934" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1360821934" />
    <a title="Will M." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20408288-will-m"><img alt="Will M." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452951660p2/20408288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1360821934?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Will M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Will M." href="/user/show/20408288-will-m">Will M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Will by: </span>
      IGN, if I remember correctly
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=marvel">marvel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/20408288-will-m?shelf=x-men">x-men</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1360821934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16553352411843953718">My love for the X-Men is not something I've hidden in the past. I've mentioned this recently, so I guess I don't really need to remind the people who read my review of another X-Men series. This first volume was great. It vaguely depicts a great story arc and hints for great plot twists to come in the next volumes. <br/><br/>The plot was different than the usual X-Men plot I got used to. I only know X-Men from the movies and I can vaguely remember some random single issues when I was younger, so I had no </span>
  <span id="freeText16553352411843953718" style="display:none">My love for the X-Men is not something I've hidden in the past. I've mentioned this recently, so I guess I don't really need to remind the people who read my review of another X-Men series. This first volume was great. It vaguely depicts a great story arc and hints for great plot twists to come in the next volumes. <br /><br />The plot was different than the usual X-Men plot I got used to. I only know X-Men from the movies and I can vaguely remember some random single issues when I was younger, so I had no idea what writers were experimenting on over the past years. Whedon had something new to offer, but it wasn't as astonishing as I would've wanted. This honestly had a really similar plot to the third X-Men movie, X-Men: The Last Stand. He changed a whole lot, but the essence was still there. The main idea was basically the same, but I'm not complaining to be honest. I just wanted to point out how similar things were, but I'm not mad because i liked X-Men: The Last Stand. I know a lot of people disliked it because the characters became darker and not jolly, but it's still the X-Men for me. The story was great, but just like the movie, this volume was also lacking. While it was great to know that there's a cure, I just seem to feel that the author has more to offer after this. I'm not completely satisfied.<br /><br />The artwork was way better than I expected. I liked how they were portrayed, unlike the most recent one I read. I know that this is just a personal preference but I always judge harshly on the artwork. Bad artwork always ruins the whole experience, so thankfully this didn't disappoint. Kudos for making Wolverine look at least cool, and even Scott Summers. Most of the time both of them look like thrash, so it's a great thing to finally pay some respect and portray them well.<br /><br />Can I just ask though, if it's too spoilery then please tell me and don't answer, but where the fuck is Storm?<br /><br />4.5.5 stars. Rounded down, just like any other Graphic Novel. I always round down when it comes to GN, so I guess you could also say that I judge these harsher than novels. A great read though, so don't hesitate to try if you're looking for a great X-Men read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16553352411843953718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2810205309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2810205309" />
    <a title="Anthony Sicoli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82164281-anthony-sicoli"><img alt="Anthony Sicoli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547648640p2/82164281.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2810205309?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony Sicoli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony Sicoli" href="/user/show/82164281-anthony-sicoli">Anthony Sicoli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82164281-anthony-sicoli?shelf=marvel_comics">marvel_comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82164281-anthony-sicoli?shelf=x-men">x-men</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2810205309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15346163852105973670"><b>Score:</b> 4.04 out of 5<br/><b>Grade:</b> 81% (A-) | Great<br/><br/>The X-Crew aim to <i>astonish</i> the world while a mutant cure causes some to question who they really are. Here is my review of <b>Astonishing X-Men Vol. 1: Gifted:</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558961440i/27578435.jpg' width='350' height='500' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>The Good:</b><br/><br/>I really liked the roster of this team – the former villain (Emma Frost), former thug (Wolverine), the leader (Cyclops), the gentle beast (Beast), and the poster child (Shadowcat) – almost like <b>the Breakfast Club of X-Men</b>. They all have their role as they try to astonish the world similar t</span>
  <span id="freeText15346163852105973670" style="display:none"><b>Score:</b> 4.04 out of 5<br><b>Grade:</b> 81% (A-) | Great<br><br>The X-Crew aim to <i>astonish</i> the world while a mutant cure causes some to question who they really are. Here is my review of <b>Astonishing X-Men Vol. 1: Gifted:</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558961440i/27578435.jpg" width="350" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The Good:</b><br><br>I really liked the roster of this team – the former villain (Emma Frost), former thug (Wolverine), the leader (Cyclops), the gentle beast (Beast), and the poster child (Shadowcat) – almost like <b>the Breakfast Club of X-Men</b>. They all have their role as they try to astonish the world similar to the likes of the Fantastic Four or the Avengers. Not everyone gets along, so conflict erupts in entertaining fashion, which means get your popcorn ready people!<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558961440i/27578436._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The book is at its best when the whole team is just sh**-talking each other. Whedon is a master at bringing ensembles together and making it work (anyone seen the Avengers…?). The humour grounds the story and makes it feel more <b>genuine and authentic</b>. I also fell in love with the art style. My favourite had to be Beast’s design. Oftentimes he just looks like a big blue fur ball, but Cassidy absolutely nails it here! The art in general is very clean n’ crisp and just beautiful to look at.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558961440i/27578437.jpg" width="250" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>The ongoing theme in this book questions who we are versus what society wants us to be. Do we follow societal norms to fit in with everyone else? Or do we accept ourselves the way we are? It’s an interesting concept that a couple of X-men ask themselves. I’ve also never heard of this Ord character before and thought he’d end up being lame, but I was wrong! It was <b>refreshing not to get another Magneto rehash</b> of the same ol’ <i>“Homo superiors &gt; Homo sapiens”</i> thing. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558961440i/27578438._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>The Bad:</b><br><br>This story suffers from a few clichés that are used to push the story forward. It didn’t ruin anything for me, but some situations just <b>end up coincidentally working out</b> for our heroes. The “just in time” clichés are what really bother me, and it happens a couple times in here. We also see the return of an X-Men and, probably because I’m not familiar with the events that happened before this book, it really didn’t do much for me.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558961440i/27578439._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>This book wraps up everyone’s story rather quickly and Ord’s demise was a little rushed. It felt like Ord’s defeat was almost a little too easy. We also get a bunch of little <b>tidbits for the upcoming storylines</b> which makes this feel more like a set-up than a standalone story. Sure these tidbits peaked my interest, but I would have preferred it more if they spent less time on these tidbits and more time fleshing out the conclusion.<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1558961440i/27578440._SX540_.png" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>Conclusion:</b><br><br>This is an excellent refreshing start to the X-Men and I’m excited to see where things go. The characters are fun, the story is exciting, the art is great – not much else you can ask for from a comic book. Consider me … *puts on cool sunglasses* … <b>
  <i>astonished.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558961440ra/27578441.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15346163852105973670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_826996101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/826996101" />
    <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar"><img alt="Dirk Grobbelaar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545117991p2/3102740.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/826996101?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dirk Grobbelaar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dirk Grobbelaar" href="/user/show/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar">Dirk Grobbelaar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=acquired-in-2014">acquired-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3102740-dirk-grobbelaar?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer826996101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4991082620733754073">This was a bit better. I’ve doggedly been trying to get aboard the X-Men bandwagon. The “Ultimate” version was too contrived for my taste, and many readers recommended Josh Whedon’s <i>Astonishing X-Men</i> run. I will admit that this is probably required reading for X-Men fans; it <b>is</b> quite good, but perhaps not the best place for the uninitiated to start. I was a bit out of my depth here. For example, I never read the arc where Colossus “died”. Professor Xavier is also missing from this outing, leavin</span>
  <span id="freeText4991082620733754073" style="display:none">This was a bit better. I’ve doggedly been trying to get aboard the X-Men bandwagon. The “Ultimate” version was too contrived for my taste, and many readers recommended Josh Whedon’s <i>Astonishing X-Men</i> run. I will admit that this is probably required reading for X-Men fans; it <b>is</b> quite good, but perhaps not the best place for the uninitiated to start. I was a bit out of my depth here. For example, I never read the arc where Colossus “died”. Professor Xavier is also missing from this outing, leaving Cyclops and Emma Frost (sort of) in charge. Neither of the two are characters I particularly care for, so…<br /><br />I quite liked Ord, the Extra Terrestrial villain. I’m hoping that, should I continue reading this series, that we’ll be seeing more of him. I would like some more insight into his hatred of mutants.<br /> Now, although <i>Gifted</i> is rather good, there are one or two scenes that venture dangerously close to being schmaltzy. If you do already like the X-Men, though, and know enough of the back story, this series is well worth your time.<br /><br />I read X-Men comics as a kid, and I enjoyed them, but I’m struggling to recapture that vibe. I’ll still check out Grant Morrison’s version, but I think what I’m really after is the stuff from the late 80s / early 90s, where Beast at least <b>looked</b> dangerous and not like a plush toy. I need a nudge in the right direction though, as far as the collected editions are concerned, since there are so <b>many</b> of them. <br /><br />….or, alternatively, I should just stick to reading <b>Wolverine</b>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4991082620733754073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1668378395" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1668378395" />
    <a title="Terence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23206148-terence"><img alt="Terence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473945175p2/23206148.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1668378395?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2016</a>

  <span id="freeText5189945563294019217" style="display:none">The X-Men are re-forming and opening Xavier's School again. Whedon likes to set major plans that can't be bothered with keeping the characters and story interesting until he gets there. It's easy to see major events are being set, but the current story telling isn't all that compelling for me.<br><br>Gifted was an OK story, but I'm in no rush to continue the series at this point.</span>

<div id="review_398110103" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/398110103" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/398110103?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=personal-mythology">personal-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=comic-books">comic-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=astonishing">astonishing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=marvel-comics">marvel-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=pb-and-j-dipped-in-hot-chocolate">pb-and-j-dipped-in-hot-chocolate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=i-named-my-daughter">i-named-my-daughter</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer398110103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3787433122834372832">My introduction to the X-Men, many years ago, was the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/103111.X_Men_The_Dark_Phoenix_Saga' title='X-Men The Dark Phoenix Saga by Chris Claremont' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dark Phoenix Saga</a> (even though it was already a couple of years old when I found it). Up until then I'd been consuming Namor and the staples: Batman, Superman, Captain America, Spiderman. My starting place was not a bad place to start; it was, in fact, a pretty fine place to start. Maybe too fine. Starting with one of the finest chapters of the X-Men might be why I've mostly been a passing fan of Marvel's mutants over the years. Nothing could</span>
  <span id="freeText3787433122834372832" style="display:none">My introduction to the X-Men, many years ago, was the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/103111.X_Men_The_Dark_Phoenix_Saga" title="X-Men The Dark Phoenix Saga by Chris Claremont" rel="nofollow noopener">Dark Phoenix Saga</a> (even though it was already a couple of years old when I found it). Up until then I'd been consuming Namor and the staples: Batman, Superman, Captain America, Spiderman. My starting place was not a bad place to start; it was, in fact, a pretty fine place to start. Maybe too fine. Starting with one of the finest chapters of the X-Men might be why I've mostly been a passing fan of Marvel's mutants over the years. Nothing could quite live up to the excellence of the Chris Claremont &amp; John Byrne partnership.<br /><br />I'd pop into the X-Men for a visit if I heard an arc was worth reading or if a crossover made a visit essential, or even buy a mini-series with an X-Man I liked, but I was never an avid reader. <br /><br />I had no idea until recently that my introduction to the X-Men was as significant to my personal mythology as it was and is, but somewhere in my squishy brain bits that first moment with the X-Men planted some seeds that germinated into my contribution to our youngest daughter's name. <br /><br />When I chose the name nine years ago (a name which was supposed to be my son Milos' when he and his twin sister Bronte were born, but he was a boy, "Damn it!" and he screwed up my plans), everyone wondered why I would chose a name like the one I chose, especially when I instantly replaced it with a nickname. I couldn't provide an answer beyond, "I dunno. I've always just loved those names." The name and the nickname felt right.<br /><br />It took <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18015.Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon" rel="nofollow noopener">Joss Whedon</a>'s* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31979.Astonishing_X_Men__Vol__1_Gifted" title="Astonishing X-Men, Vol. 1 Gifted by Joss Whedon" rel="nofollow noopener">Astonishing X-Men Vol. 1 Gifted</a> to answer that question and reveal the roots of the brain shrub that had been growing since I was a kid, but the answer was there in the pages of his epic X-Collaboration with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12775.John_Cassaday" title="John Cassaday" rel="nofollow noopener">John Cassaday</a>. <br /><br />As soon as I started reading I was greeted by an old, old friend -- Shadowcat. She's late for her return to Professor Xavier's School for Gifted Youngsters, and she finds an empty school upon her arrival, so she starts walking through walls and sinking through floors trying to figure out where everyone's gone (she can <i>phase</i> through anything, in case you didn't know). And I am thrilled. I instantly remember how much I've loved Shadowcat through the years, and I hope that she'll bump into Wolverine soon (in the movies, Rogue's relationship with Wolvie is based on the comic book relationship between him and Shadowcat). Instead, she stumbles into a school assembly and shrugs off the embarrassment at her lateness when the new Headmistress, Emma Frost (former White Queen of the Hellfire Club), mocks her. She gives Emma a sassy tongue lashing and reminds the White Queen that the first time they met Emma tried to kill her, derailing her search for the X-Men and unleashing a Dark Phoenix. I snort at Shadowcat's telling blow, then remember that Dark Phoenix was indeed the first appearance of Kitty Pryde. <br /><br />And I start to wonder without any serious thought whether "Kitty" has anything to do with my Kitty Kat's nickname; something is shaking those roots, but I ignore it and keep reading until it comes clear. <br /><br />You see ... another old favourite appears right near the end<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Colossus, resurrected from the dead by alien baddy, Ord <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and he calls Kitty by the name only he calls her -- "Katya" -- and I know the source of my contribution to Scoutie's name: Katya Gwendolyn Scout. I should have known all along, but somehow the source slipped away from me only to be revealed in the best X-Man comic since the Dark Phoenix Saga.<br /><br />I think they're fabulous. Both the comic and the revelation it catalyzed. And I love comics. And Joss Whedon. And most of all I love my Scoutie Kat. <br /><br />*For all you oldsters out there: did you know that Joss Whedon's Dad, Tom Whedon, was the head writer for The Electric Company? How fucking cool is that?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3787433122834372832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10804238100190834939">After the monotonous Marvel comics I have read recently, this is a breath of fresh air. This has characters and it doesn't feel like it's simply about the action. I was engaged and it was fun. Why can't this be more of what the comics are doing. Joss is amazing and he really does understand emotions and characters. That's what he does.<br/><br/>I love the art. I thought the plot was fun without being too ridiculous. I mean there is an alien in it and it's only one and it does overwhelm the story. There is</span>
  <span id="freeText10804238100190834939" style="display:none">After the monotonous Marvel comics I have read recently, this is a breath of fresh air. This has characters and it doesn't feel like it's simply about the action. I was engaged and it was fun. Why can't this be more of what the comics are doing. Joss is amazing and he really does understand emotions and characters. That's what he does.<br /><br />I love the art. I thought the plot was fun without being too ridiculous. I mean there is an alien in it and it's only one and it does overwhelm the story. There is a lot of back story I have obviously missed before this started. Oh well. <br /><br />I was entertained with a quick read. </span>

<div id="review_1841922582" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1841922582" />
    <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren"><img alt="Wren (fablesandwren)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596719528p2/42780417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1841922582?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wren (fablesandwren)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wren (fablesandwren)" href="/user/show/42780417-wren-fablesandwren">Wren (fablesandwren)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=04-stars">04-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42780417-wren-fablesandwren?shelf=not-shelved">not-shelved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1841922582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11977685450687246820">So, I think I mistook this volume. I thought I was reading the first ever issue of X-Men, when really this is just another whole set of X-Men. I knew that there were multiple sets and stories and characters and such, because you hear people talking about how "in one alternate universe this happened which is different from this other universe" and such and so forth.<br/><br/>BUT, it wasn't that confusing. Because I knew the characters and I knew about the girl who is already dead in the beginning (it's Jea</span>
  <span id="freeText11977685450687246820" style="display:none">So, I think I mistook this volume. I thought I was reading the first ever issue of X-Men, when really this is just another whole set of X-Men. I knew that there were multiple sets and stories and characters and such, because you hear people talking about how "in one alternate universe this happened which is different from this other universe" and such and so forth.<br><br>BUT, it wasn't that confusing. Because I knew the characters and I knew about the girl who is already dead in the beginning (it's Jean. It isn't a spoiler. Stop freaking out. Just stop). <br><br>And again, BUT the two X-Men movies that we have are kind of mixed into one in this. The whole "cure for the mutants" didn't happen while Jean through her fit and went kind of crazy. Emma Frost (that girl from the other X-Men movie that has diamond skin and can read minds) is in this and is actually playing for the good guys now, even though I sense she had a past.<br><br>Oh and don't forget to throw a little Avengers in there with a Agent Fury.<br><br>We start off with Kitty (girl who can walk through walls). She is joining the remaining X-Men (Logan/Wolverine, Hank/Beast, Summers/Cyclops and Emma Frost) to help young mutant kids come to turns with their powers and who they are. <br><br>Well, there's this weird alien that wants to kill all mutants and there's also a doctor lady who claims to have found a cure. <br><br>So sure, let's put together a bunch of people who don't like each other and then throw actual problems at them. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514833314i/24813076.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="263" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The artistry is wonderful and brilliant, even though some costumes are so unrealistic I just roll my eyes *cough* Frost *cough*. The story had a lot of snarky comics and funny pieces, like the image above was suppose to be.. well, without giving anything away, it was suppose to be Hawaii but it was forgotten that they were a lot bigger. <br><br>I could tell who people were just by what they looked like (since I have watched the movies religiously since I was in high school). The characters have a lot of edges and angles to them, and you know that you are just about to see another level to them. They all have history together which is kind of fun to dig into it.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1514833314i/24813077.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="229" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Also, Wolverine is forever my forever.<br><br>I am obviously going to annoy the crap out of all my followers and friends here and continue on with this set of "Astonishing X-Men," but I will try to space them out some so you don't end up hating me too much.<br><br>Side note: I am looking for other awesome graphic novels / comics. So if you have any you love and you want someone else to love, comment below or message me! I would love to check them out!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11977685450687246820" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_344516150" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/344516150" />
    <a title="Sam Quixote" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote"><img alt="Sam Quixote" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529183438p2/5759543.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/344516150?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam Quixote" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam Quixote" href="/user/show/5759543-sam-quixote">Sam Quixote</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer344516150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12205048679468145856">Picking up where Grant Morrison left off, Joss Whedon begins his run on the X-Men with a new line up consisting of Cyclops, Emma Frost, Beast, Kitty Pryde, Lockheed the X-Dragon, and Wolverine (Xavier is "on sabbatical"). He's also reinstated the classic superhero outfits, ditching Morrison and Quitely's additions of black leather as "it was spooking people".<br/><br/>Having seen the third X-Men movie long before picking up this book I noticed the storyline they used in that film being used here for the f</span>
  <span id="freeText12205048679468145856" style="display:none">Picking up where Grant Morrison left off, Joss Whedon begins his run on the X-Men with a new line up consisting of Cyclops, Emma Frost, Beast, Kitty Pryde, Lockheed the X-Dragon, and Wolverine (Xavier is "on sabbatical"). He's also reinstated the classic superhero outfits, ditching Morrison and Quitely's additions of black leather as "it was spooking people".<br /><br />Having seen the third X-Men movie long before picking up this book I noticed the storyline they used in that film being used here for the first time - a cure for the mutant gene. Whedon came up with this great idea and full credit to him for making it both emotional and intellectual rather than simply another threat to be beaten up with mutant powers.<br /><br />Beast especially is a tragic case as his appearance has always bothered him and for a chance to reverse that... well I won't give away what he decides. Suffice it to say this story has heart, something rare in superhero comics. But it's Whedon so there's plenty of fun moments and jokes to make this a great read.<br /><br />Artist John Cassady is one of comics' best living artists and his work here is no less amazing as it was on "Planetary". His Kitty Pryde in particular is very good, though there's no character he doesn't do justice to.<br /><br />I've watched Buffy, Firefly, and of course The Avengers, but this is the first Joss Whedon I've read and I'm pleasantly surprised by his high level of writing ability translating off screen and on the comics page. "Gifted" is an excellent start to an imaginative and fully realised X-Men storyline that I'll be looking forward to reading more of. Recommended for all X-fans. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12205048679468145856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

That'll keep 'em on their toes for a while.<br/><br/>Loving the super-bitch Emma Frost that Whedon cooked up - he really does have a way with female characters doesn't he?<br/><br/>The writing and art are a nice, fresh yet familiar take on our favourite misfits. <div id="review_185708265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185708265" />
    <a title="Ronyell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell"><img alt="Ronyell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506581787p2/1169488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185708265?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ronyell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ronyell" href="/user/show/1169488-ronyell">Ronyell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=russian-hero-or-heroine">russian-hero-or-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=modern-age-comics">modern-age-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=ronyell-s-epinions-reviews">ronyell-s-epinions-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=marvel-comics">marvel-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=canadian-hero-or-heroine">canadian-hero-or-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=my-blog-reviews">my-blog-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=graphic-novels-comics">graphic-novels-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1169488-ronyell?shelf=joss-whedon">joss-whedon</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer185708265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9479617428519244436"><b>Review is also on:</b> <a href='http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/01/astonishing-x-men-gifted-by-joss-whedon.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a> <br/><br/><i>
  <b>6 stars!</b>
</i><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Brief History:</u>
</b><br/><br/>Alright, I have actually first heard of the “X-Men” series when I was little and it was through a 90s cartoon series entitled “X-Men: The Animated Series.” From that day on, I was so hooked onto the “X-Men” franchise that I practically watched every incarnation of “X-Men” throughout my life which included the animated series “X-Men: Evolution” and I even watched all three “X-Men” movies. Now the truth of the matter is that ev</span>
  <span id="freeText9479617428519244436" style="display:none"><b>Review is also on:</b> <a href="http://rabbitearsbookblog.blogspot.com/2012/01/astonishing-x-men-gifted-by-joss-whedon.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabbit Ears Book Blog</a> <br /><br /><i>
  <b>6 stars!</b>
</i><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Brief History:</u>
</b><br /><br />Alright, I have actually first heard of the “X-Men” series when I was little and it was through a 90s cartoon series entitled “X-Men: The Animated Series.” From that day on, I was so hooked onto the “X-Men” franchise that I practically watched every incarnation of “X-Men” throughout my life which included the animated series “X-Men: Evolution” and I even watched all three “X-Men” movies. Now the truth of the matter is that even though I have heard of the “X-Men” franchise ever since I was a child, I never read the comics at all, until now. I never read the comics before because there was just too many universes involving everyone's favorite superhero mutants and I am one of those people who cannot keep up with too many different versions of certain characters' lives because I will get confused easily. Well, I stumbled upon this unique comic book from the “X-Men” series entitled “Astonishing X-Men: Gifted” and when I found out that Joss Whedon (creator of “Buffy the Vampire Slayer”) was going to write an “X-Men” comic, I was shocked and excited at the same time! Joss Whedon is surely an accomplished writer and I have watched “Buffy the Vampire Slayer” before and I really enjoyed that show! And now, without further ado, I will now discuss about what this book is all about and my opinions on this comic.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What is the story?</u>
</b><br /><br />Cyclops and Emma Frost, who are now in charge of the institute, started reforming the X-Men once again to prove to the world that even though they are mutants, they are the heroes and they want to “astonish” the world with their heroic deeds. However, when a mutant cure reaches all over the world and many mutants line up to get the cure, will the X-Men's efforts to prove to the world that they are the good guys fall in vain? And to add to that, the X-Men will soon reunite with a fellow mutant who was presumed dead. Who is that mutant? Find out once you pick up “Astonishing X-Men: Gifted!”<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What I loved about this comic:</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><u>Joss Whedon's writing:</u> Joss Whedon's writing was so brilliant in this comic! He really knows how to bring excitement and suspense to the storyline regarding the X-Men trying to figure out the secrets of this “mutant cure” and who is behind all of this commotion. I also loved the way that Joss Whedon is able to shock the audience with various scenes that came so unexpected in the story, such as the scene where we find out about the mutant who was presumed dead and when I found out about that situation, I was totally shocked beyond all reason and yet I was extremely happy to see how the shock of this scene was written and shown. I also loved the way that Joss Whedon incorporated humor into the story at the right places, like Wolverine's obsession with beer and that one popular line in the book where Wolverine is cursing like crazy and you just see a bunch of symbols indicating the strong language.<br /><br /><u>John Cassaday's illustrations:</u> John Cassaday's illustrations were simply gorgeous and fitted this story perfectly. I loved how all the X-Men characters look so real and I especially loved seeing their expressions that ranged from anger to shock as it was amusing to look at. I also loved the lighting of certain scenes such as the X-Men going to the Benetech lab and everything inside the lab is shaded in green which fitted the brooding mood of the lab.<br /><br /><u>The characters:</u> I have never seen such amazing characters from the “X-Men” universe in my entire life! All the characters were interesting without being boring at all and I loved seeing the actual conflicts they have with each other, especially between Emma Frost and Kitty Pryde as they clearly have contempt for each other due to Emma's horrible past. Even though I will always be a Cyclops/Jean Grey fan, I thought that the relationship between Emma and Scott was pretty interesting and they seem to share some kind of bond that I never would have seen in any other comic. I also loved the fact that Kitty Pryde seems to be the star of this issue since the media rarely focuses on her character and what was so interesting about her character was that she resembled Buffy from “Buffy the Vampire Slayer” in being the heroic heroine who would do anything to save her friends from disaster.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>What made me feel uncomfortable about this book:</u>
</b><br /><br />I do not really have much of a problem with this issue since I thought it was perfect, but for those of you who do not like gore and language, this volume contains plenty of gore and language, so I would probably not read this issue if language and violence is a bother to some people.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Final Thoughts:</u>
</b><br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed reading “Astonishing X-Men: Gifted” and I am looking forward to reading up on the next issue “Dangerous” from this fantastic series! If anyone has ever read the “X-Men” series before and you want to recommend me some titles, please recommend me some “X-Men” titles that were really great to read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9479617428519244436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_267570670" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267570670" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267570670?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=superhumans">superhumans</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267570670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5876375945203630835">There was no question in my mind that Joss Whedon can write, and quite well at that. But can he write the X-Men? The answer, of course, is that he can, and quite well at that.<br/><br/>This is, I believe, the first X book I've picked up in probably eight years. Nightcrawler is my favorite, and between <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[retconning his origin in the most stupid way possible and killing him off <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I've been avoiding them as unnecessary stressors. But that means that I missed Whedon's run on Astonis</span>
  <span id="freeText5876375945203630835" style="display:none">There was no question in my mind that Joss Whedon can write, and quite well at that. But can he write the X-Men? The answer, of course, is that he can, and quite well at that.<br /><br />This is, I believe, the first X book I've picked up in probably eight years. Nightcrawler is my favorite, and between <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[retconning his origin in the most stupid way possible and killing him off <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I've been avoiding them as unnecessary stressors. But that means that I missed Whedon's run on Astonishing X-Men, and that's just a travesty. This is just about as good as it gets. The plot is tight, consistent, and raises interesting questions. (There's a possible "cure" for mutants- now what?) The characterization is spot on, hell, better than most outings these characters have had. I think I might actually like Scott Summers in this book, and I don't know if I can process that. The dialog is natural, neither corny, preachy, or overly wordy, and there's humor. There's an emotional climax to this particular book that's written with a sincerity that made it affecting.<br /><br />And the art! Do you know how many times I've picked up X books only to see that the artist gave every woman the exact same face? It's just so nice to see good art in an X book.<br /><br />I can only think of one specific complaint, which is that Whedon didn't use Nightcrawler. I want to see him write Nightcrawler. Yes, this is selfish of me, but I think I'm allowed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5876375945203630835" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_920358406" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/920358406?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Marvel/X-Men/Joss Whedon fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=school-days">school-days</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2014-graphic-novel-reading-challeng">2014-graphic-novel-reading-challeng</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2014-action-adventure-aficionados-c">2014-action-adventure-aficionados-c</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=superhuman">superhuman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2014-cover-to-cover-challenge">2014-cover-to-cover-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920358406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14597247377602471387">I have been on a Marvel roll lately. It's mainly due to the fact that I've been mainlining Marvel shows on Netflix, along with the various Marvel movies we've been treated to lately. I discovered that there was a motion comic series for The Astonishing X-Men, and some of the episodes are posted on Netflix. Watching it and "Wolverine and the X-Men" (and loving it), encouraged me to check out some of the comics after many years of not reading them. Luckily my awesome library has this series!<br/><br/>I will</span>
  <span id="freeText14597247377602471387" style="display:none">I have been on a Marvel roll lately. It's mainly due to the fact that I've been mainlining Marvel shows on Netflix, along with the various Marvel movies we've been treated to lately. I discovered that there was a motion comic series for The Astonishing X-Men, and some of the episodes are posted on Netflix. Watching it and "Wolverine and the X-Men" (and loving it), encouraged me to check out some of the comics after many years of not reading them. Luckily my awesome library has this series!<br /><br />I will admit I am an admirer of Joss Whedon's tv shows, and his characteristic wit is on display in this comic book series run that he authors. His snark and biting sarcasm, plus some sociopolitical commentary. It's fun to see his words come out of the mouth of Emma Frost, Wolverine, and the gang. Not to say it feels foreign to the X-Men, but Whedon just has a characteristic writing style.<br /><br />Along with the writing, the artwork is beautiful. Bright and stylish, but also detailed to the degree that Kitty's hair blows in the wind like real life, Wolverine's arms and back are covered in hair (let me say that he's the only guy who can get a free pass for back hair), and Emma Frost is unrealistically gorgeous, both in her flesh and diamond form (Can I admit I have a tiny girl crush on Emma Frost?). <br /><br />I thought I was over the X-Men, but I see that I am very wrong. I am definitely officially sucked back into the world of the mutants. I wish I could run back to the library today to get the next volume.<br /><br />FYI: Marvel has a wikia database that is tres awesome: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://marvel.wikia.com/Main_Page">http://marvel.wikia.com/Main_Page</a><br /><br />Overall rating: <b>4.5/5.0 stars</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14597247377602471387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_53180923" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53180923" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411956191p2/1219253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53180923?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53180923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15284050542480100807">Oh, X-Men, how do I love thee? I shall not bore anyone by counting the ways, but suffice it to say I love 'em. However, my introduction to the X-Men did not come in the form of a comic book, but instead from the Saturday morning cartoon show that used to run on FOX and, later, the big budget movies. I wasn't a comic book reader as a kid (mainly due to lack of access--there were no bookstores in my small rural town) and discovering that the X-Men had been around forever did not exactly encourage </span>
  <span id="freeText15284050542480100807" style="display:none">Oh, X-Men, how do I love thee? I shall not bore anyone by counting the ways, but suffice it to say I love 'em. However, my introduction to the X-Men did not come in the form of a comic book, but instead from the Saturday morning cartoon show that used to run on FOX and, later, the big budget movies. I wasn't a comic book reader as a kid (mainly due to lack of access--there were no bookstores in my small rural town) and discovering that the X-Men had been around forever did not exactly encourage me to begin reading. I assumed that I would have to start at the beginning and the idea of doing so was overwhelming. <br /><br />What finally inspired me to begin reading this series is that it's written by Joss Whedon (oh, Firefly, how do I love thee?). Whedon plus the X-Men is an irresistable combination. There's definitely some trademark Whedon going on here, most notably in the snappy dialogue and the clever scenes (my favorite is when Ord breaks into the school, only to find the X-Men aren't there--just the students, thus leading to an amusing "would you like to leave a message" dialogue). However, overall, it didn't grab me. I think this is mainly because the X-Men involved (Cyclops, Kitty Pryde, Beast, Emma Frost, and, of course, the ubiquitous Wolverine) just aren't among my favorites. All in all, though, it was a pretty good book and I'll definitely read the others in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15284050542480100807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2221335492" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11000806901790535053">4.5 stars<br/><br/>Ah, Kitty Pryde. I guess I think of her as an avatar for the reader with this team's line-up. We may not have Beast's intellect, Emma Frost's looks, Wolverine's toughness, or Cyclops' leadership skills, but Kitty is just Kitty (and all the better for it) - as in plucky, aware, good-hearted and dependable. <br/><br/>I thought she was one of the best things about the <i>All New X-Men</i> series that I read earlier this year, and the feeling continues with <i>Astonishing Vol. 1</i>. There was a lot of good action</span>
  <span id="freeText11000806901790535053" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />Ah, Kitty Pryde. I guess I think of her as an avatar for the reader with this team's line-up. We may not have Beast's intellect, Emma Frost's looks, Wolverine's toughness, or Cyclops' leadership skills, but Kitty is just Kitty (and all the better for it) - as in plucky, aware, good-hearted and dependable. <br /><br />I thought she was one of the best things about the <i>All New X-Men</i> series that I read earlier this year, and the feeling continues with <i>Astonishing Vol. 1</i>. There was a lot of good action, good dialogue (the spirited bickering between Kitty and Emma; Cyclops and Nick Fury; Wolverine and pretty much everyone) and a nice amount of unexpected humor, as well. As the team strutted in tandem to board the X-Jet and intervene in a hostage situation . . . well, it's just one of those little things that make superhero comic books worth reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11000806901790535053" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2588099-j-m?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2588099-j-m?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer122369745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer464042708423904817">I haven't picked up an X-Men comic in a long time, unless you count the WOLVERINE ORIGINS: DEADPOOL graphic novel I reviewed recently; example, I had no idea that Scott Summers (Cyclops) and Emma Frost (the White Queen), were a couple. When did that happen? Nevertheless, in ASTONISHING X-MEN, it works. I love the interplay between Scott and Emma, with her love for Scott sullied by her bitterness of what he once shared with Jean Grey. I also like Kitty Pryde's overt mistrust of the White Queen ow</span>
  <span id="freeText464042708423904817" style="display:none">I haven't picked up an X-Men comic in a long time, unless you count the WOLVERINE ORIGINS: DEADPOOL graphic novel I reviewed recently; example, I had no idea that Scott Summers (Cyclops) and Emma Frost (the White Queen), were a couple. When did that happen? Nevertheless, in ASTONISHING X-MEN, it works. I love the interplay between Scott and Emma, with her love for Scott sullied by her bitterness of what he once shared with Jean Grey. I also like Kitty Pryde's overt mistrust of the White Queen owing to prior bad blood.<br><br>As a fan of both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18015.Joss_Whedon" title="Joss Whedon" rel="nofollow noopener">Joss Whedon</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12775.John_Cassaday" title="John Cassaday" rel="nofollow noopener">John Cassaday</a>, I've been excited to read ASTONISHING X-MEN for quite a while. So far, though the first six issues in the "Gifted" trade paperback, I haven't been disappointed. Whedon's storyline is tight. His plot moves along at a great clip. The dialogue has just the right amount of pith and wit (say "pith and wit" five times fast -- sorta fun, huh?). <br><br>Cassaday's art is a real pleasure to soak in -- he perfectly combines heroics, drama, emotion, and realism with his masterful artistic abilities. On that last bit, realism, I'm just not into every bulging vein and corded sinew popping through a hero's costume. Cassaday has a knack for making his heroes look both heroic and real at the same time, and I love it. He's been one of my favorite comic artists going all the way back to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/254207.Desperadoes_A_Moment_s_Sunlight" title="Desperadoes A Moment's Sunlight by Jeff Mariotte" rel="nofollow noopener">DESPERADOES</a>.<br><br>The "Gifted" storyline centers around a mutant cure with the undertone of a secret alien invasion. The covert organizations of S.H.I.E.L.D. (Nick Fury!) and S.W.O.R.D. end up getting involved, and one of the more compelling parts of the story is Dr. Hank McCoy's (Beast) personal struggle, for of all the mutants in the current team -- Scott, Emma, Kitty, Logan (Wolverine) -- Hank is the one whose mutations are the most evident and unattractive, making this miracle cure a very ambiguous lure. I think this is enough of a teaser, so I won't spoil any more of this excellent series. If you haven't picked up an X-Men title lately, I recommend the ASTONISHING X-MEN. You can waltz right in, quickly get up to speed, and enjoy a quality comic series with "marvelous" art (pun intended!).<br><br>Four out of five stars. <br>--<br><br>Also check out these titles featuring John Cassaday's work:<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/209967.Absolute_Planetary_Book_One" title="Absolute Planetary Book One by Warren Ellis" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1320394322s/209967.jpg" alt="Absolute Planetary Book One by Warren Ellis" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1818336.Planetary_Batman_Night_on_Earth" title="Planetary/Batman Night on Earth by Warren Ellis" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1188769612s/1818336.jpg" alt="Planetary/Batman Night on Earth by Warren Ellis" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4705107.Desperadoes_Omnibus" title="Desperadoes Omnibus by Jeff Mariotte" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1266896027s/4705107.jpg" alt="Desperadoes Omnibus by Jeff Mariotte" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="464042708423904817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4063612617827743680">Cyclops, Beast, Wolverine, Shadowcat, and Emma Frost make up a new incarnation of the X-Men. In an effort to promote a positive profile, the team resumes its helpful "superteam" activities and stops an unexplained attack by the alien Ord of the Breakworld. Meanwhile, Doctor Kavita Rao of Benetech has just announced a cure for mutations, which doesn't sit well with the X-Men. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[The mysterious Ord and Dr. Rao are connected in their motives and are in fact working together: Ord believe</span></span>
  <span id="freeText4063612617827743680" style="display:none">Cyclops, Beast, Wolverine, Shadowcat, and Emma Frost make up a new incarnation of the X-Men. In an effort to promote a positive profile, the team resumes its helpful "superteam" activities and stops an unexplained attack by the alien Ord of the Breakworld. Meanwhile, Doctor Kavita Rao of Benetech has just announced a cure for mutations, which doesn't sit well with the X-Men. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The mysterious Ord and Dr. Rao are connected in their motives and are in fact working together: Ord believes an X-Man will destroy his homeworld in three years and so wants to eliminate mutants, and Rao genuinely wants to help those adversely affected by mutation by using Ord's tech. The whole enterprise is being supported by S.W.O.R.D., the parallel organization to S.H.I.E.L.D. that counters extraterrestrial threats, in order to avoid an interstellar war with Breakworld. It's revealed that the formerly dead X-Man Colossus is alive and has been a captive of Ord for years. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Joss Whedon's first X-Men arc is exciting and funny, several plot threads are brought together effortlessly, and the team dynamic is so well done that this feels almost like a quintessential roster. Despite some references to previous events, this does seem like a good jumping on point for readers new to the X-Men, though there are plenty of elements that will entertain old fans.</span>

Removed from the twisted continuity and stories of the present X-men comics, this series approached the team in some general present time in the marvel universe and created a simpler context with which to follow a very entertaining story. This review applies to all of the volumes, even thought the third is my favorite hence far. I am greatly anticipating the (spoiled) ending of Joss' run in volume four.</span>
